  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d77cb235-bc12-4400-b736-ed70075b978b'
      });
    }

His search for answers leads him toward the mountains -- the home of the Tribe of Rushing Water. Lionpaw and Hollypaw feel drawn to the mountains too, for different reasons.<br /><br />But the mountains hide secrets as well as answers, and if the three cats find a way to get there, they may discover more than they ever expected.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972822245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9860250653942360295">Cultures collide. I was waiting for Jaypaw to dream up a Tribe solution at the end rather than the Clan solution that emerged. Then it turned out that the whole thing had occurred just because the three (two of whom don't even know about the prophecy yet) had to go to the mountains and be damned to the Tribe! And I am unclear what the three were to learn - or did learn - after going there. Still enjoyable but sometimes seems like there is little point in it?</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159697311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159697311" />
    <a title="Micheline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline"><img alt="Micheline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520260852p2/4845030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159697311?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Micheline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micheline" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline">Micheline</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=creature-characters">creature-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer159697311&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159697311" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13528436006485079017">The Power of Three series seems to get more compelling as we learn more and more about 'The Chosen Three's' powers, skills and as they themselves mature, and Outcast is definitely no exception. In book 3 of the PO3 series, the surviving original members of the journey to Sun-Drown place: BrambleClaw, SquirrelFlight, CrowFeather & TawnyPelt set off to help the tribe of the mountains that they had encountered in 'The New Prophecy series'. The twist is this time, the original cats of the 1st journe</span>
  <span id="freeText13528436006485079017" style="display:none">The Power of Three series seems to get more compelling as we learn more and more about 'The Chosen Three's' powers, skills and as they themselves mature, and Outcast is definitely no exception. In book 3 of the PO3 series, the surviving original members of the journey to Sun-Drown place: BrambleClaw, SquirrelFlight, CrowFeather &amp; TawnyPelt set off to help the tribe of the mountains that they had encountered in 'The New Prophecy series'. The twist is this time, the original cats of the 1st journey take their children, who are now apprentices with them. JayPaw is certain that the Tribe will offer answers about the ominous prophecy regarding himself, his sister and brother. Despite HollyPaw &amp; LionPaw not being aware of the prophecy surrounding them, still find that they too are drawn to the mountains...but their journey there, and the answers they find are not necessarily what they expect...<br /><br />As usual Erin Hunter wastes no time on repetitive details reminding the reader of things they already know, she just dives right in with the action, plot twists and while some secrets are revealed, others still lay undiscovered, and the suspense is killing me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13528436006485079017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1597384301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1597384301" />
    <a title="Kate Matson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37293133-kate-matson"><img alt="Kate Matson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474053243p2/37293133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597384301?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Matson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Matson" href="/user/show/37293133-kate-matson">Kate Matson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062367105" href="/book/show/23367399-outcast">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37293133-kate-matson?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597384301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer419900890989842079">Summary:<br/>There will be three, Kin of you kin....Who hold the Power of the stars In their paws. A secret prophecy shapes the lives of Firestar's grandchildren, but only one of the three knows about it. Jaypaw is captivated by the power it promises, and he believes the key to that power may lie buried in the distant past -- with the ancient cats who once walked these woods and now prowl through his dreams.His search for answers leads him toward the mountains -- the home of the Tribe of Rushing Wate</span>
  <span id="freeText419900890989842079" style="display:none">Summary:<br />There will be three, Kin of you kin....Who hold the Power of the stars In their paws. A secret prophecy shapes the lives of Firestar's grandchildren, but only one of the three knows about it. Jaypaw is captivated by the power it promises, and he believes the key to that power may lie buried in the distant past -- with the ancient cats who once walked these woods and now prowl through his dreams.His search for answers leads him toward the mountains -- the home of the Tribe of Rushing Water. Lionpaw and Hollypaw feel drawn to the mountains too, for different reasons. But the mountains hide secrets as well as answers, and if the three cats find a way to get there, they may discover more than they ever expected.<br />Plot:<br />I had automatically raised my hopes for this book, given that Warrior books get better and better as they go. Unfortunately, this was barely any better than the previous books in the Power of Three series. Don't get me wrong, it had a great plot, but there wasn't any it-blew-my-mind surprises in the plot. It was the same-ol' warrior book, expect them helping in the mountains. The ending had to have been my favorite part. Not about the battle (that part was boring), but about Jaypaw talking to his litter-mates. I admit, it wasn't an exciting ending, but it made me really want to know what happens next. <br />Characters:<br />Even though there wasn't any character development, off the bat Jaypaw was loads better. He didn't have a major attitude, and was actually concerned about other cats. Again, Hollypaw didn't really play a mandatory part. I still really enjoyed her P.O.V., and I'm 100% sure that she'll play an important part in the future, but as of right now, she's just an unnecessary cat (Even though she's my absolute favorite!). Lionpaw is still being haunted by Tigerstar. Although, not near as much in this book. I wish Tigerstar would just stay in the Dark Forest where he belongs. It was cool at first for him to be haunting cats, but after 3, it's just old news. <br />Overall &amp; Recommendations:<br />I'm pretty sure everything I just said above was negative, but I still really liked this book. The ending was great, and I can see in the near future the prophecy coming into play. The entire Warrior series is amazing, and I recommend it to everybody. </span>
  <a data-text-id="419900890989842079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17678390861002081839">This was a book that definitely picked up the pace of the PO3 series as each of Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw's litter begin to embrace, develop, and understand their gifts.   <span id="freeText17678390861002081839" style="display:none">This was a book that definitely picked up the pace of the PO3 series as each of Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw's litter begin to embrace, develop, and understand their gifts. However, we learn much about Jaypaw as his curiousity takes him on a dreamquest to weave a tapestry from the tattered dreams he has shared, as well as invaded, with StarClan, the Tribe of Endless Hunting, and the Ancient Cats. <br /><br />The three of this prophesy all find themselves drawn to the mountains but for different reasons ... and through a strange twist of fate, find themselves on a quest to help the Tribe of Rushing Water in its our of need ... despite the Tribe's wishes against that. The remaining members of the original journey to the Sun Drowned place all reunite in this quest, along with Crowfether's son, Breezepaw, who displays his father's original negativity during this rescue adventure.<br /><br />An excellent third book in the series that leaves the reader with a closing cliffhanger that will whet the appetite to move right into the 4th book in the PO3 Series, "Eclipse." Make sure you have a copy handy and ready to go ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17678390861002081839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16969728457766732505">The book Warriors Outcast by Erin Hunter is a amazing. This mysterious prophecy “There will be three, Kin of your kin Who hold the Power of the stars In their paws,” is known by one cat. Even though three cats will fulfill the prophecy, one cat knows about it, Jaypaw, he is the medicine cat apprentice, so he gets a lot of dreams. He doesn't just get dreams, but he also has powers. Jaypaw thinks the answers to this prophecy lies in the past, with the ancient cats. The search for answers led Jaypa</span>
  <span id="freeText16969728457766732505" style="display:none">The book Warriors Outcast by Erin Hunter is a amazing. This mysterious prophecy “There will be three, Kin of your kin Who hold the Power of the stars In their paws,” is known by one cat. Even though three cats will fulfill the prophecy, one cat knows about it, Jaypaw, he is the medicine cat apprentice, so he gets a lot of dreams. He doesn't just get dreams, but he also has powers. Jaypaw thinks the answers to this prophecy lies in the past, with the ancient cats. The search for answers led Jaypaw towards the mountains, the mountains hide secrets, but also answers.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3039728454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3039728454" />
    <a title="Historyprincess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess"><img alt="Historyprincess" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3039728454?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Historyprincess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Historyprincess" href="/user/show/12881308-historyprincess">Historyprincess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30457482-outcast">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12881308-historyprincess?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3039728454&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3039728454" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12055670991042795122">Premise: Having just barely prevented all-out war between ThunderClan and WindClan, Lionpaw, Hollypaw, and Jaypaw find themselves drawn to the mountains – each for their own reasons. When two desperate cats arrive to plead for help on behalf of the Tribe of Rushing Water, the three siblings leap at the chance to see the world beyond their home. But even as they struggle to provide aid to the ailing Tribe, more important discoveries await the apprentices – ones that could challenge their understa</span>
  <span id="freeText12055670991042795122" style="display:none">Premise: Having just barely prevented all-out war between ThunderClan and WindClan, Lionpaw, Hollypaw, and Jaypaw find themselves drawn to the mountains – each for their own reasons. When two desperate cats arrive to plead for help on behalf of the Tribe of Rushing Water, the three siblings leap at the chance to see the world beyond their home. But even as they struggle to provide aid to the ailing Tribe, more important discoveries await the apprentices – ones that could challenge their understanding of history, their ancestors, and themselves.<br /><br />Story/Writing: Just before I start this review, I'd like to say that this book took me a little longer to read than usual because of two big things happening in my day-to-day life and my own lack of sleep. I'm pretty sure my understanding of this book and my feelings about it are still firm, but they might be a little fuzzier this time around. With that said, wow… I know I may have said this before in other reviews but, this book truly blew my mind. Reading this book truly opened my mind about how much time and care the authors put into crafting their world and its history. Given that I've been reading these books in chronological order, and that I still remember things I learned years ago when I first heard about the series, I might know certain things that I'm not technically supposed to when I read particular books. But it just goes to show how well these books are written that I learned things (or rather, put certain things together) that I did not see coming. For example, I already know the Tribe and the Clans are connected having read the "Dawn of the Clans" arc. But I also wondered why StarClan would send the Clans to this specific area around the lake if they'd never been to it themselves. Then when I got to certain parts in the book, I remembered things from the "Dawn of the Clans" arc, and when I put it all together, my mind was just blown. I know this is a spoiler-filled review but I'd like for you to figure it for yourself nonetheless! Not to mention, the way the prophecy plays into the events that happen in this book really surprised me. In the hands of a lesser author (or authors), it would come across as too obvious. But the Erin Hunter team did it in such a subtle way that I only figured out their intentions by the end, and it was exhilarating!<br /><br />Characters: What actually happens in this book is of course made all the better given that we experience it all through these fantastically written characters. The Erin Hunter team does such a good job on finding ways to help characters grow and do it convincingly. Particularly with the three siblings, see through their points of view and feel what they feel. And while the books are written in third-person, I don't think it would be much different if it was in first-person. I guess the best way I can describe it is watching yourself on camera or in a dream. You may not be experiencing what's going on at the moment, but you know what you were/are thinking and feeling nonetheless.<br /><br />Jaypaw – I once again consider Jaypaw the main character in this book, even though he's not on the cover, because his quest to me feels the most important. And while I still feel Hollypaw is the most similar to me, there are plenty of things about her brother that I have in common with as well. For example, he likes his privacy and often thinks of loftier things than most cats, and not just because he's a medicine cat. He also sees (no pun intended) and pays attention to things and details that most cats, even other medicine cats, would ignore. Even though I knew or had figured out things that he was only just learning about, it was nonetheless a thrill to read about him making these discoveries. I even felt his frustration when he hit roadblocks in his search for answers. He's the only one who knows of the prophecy (until the end, at least), aside from Firestar to whom it was given. Most cats (especially young ones) would probably just take something like that at face value, but Jaypaw has always (from what I've read so far, anyway) been about digging to find hidden truths and meanings beneath the surface, even if he's sometimes a bit too eager about it. But aside from that, when he discovers the stick that used to belong to Rock and is far older than it looks, he can't help but wonder if the cats from back then are somehow connected to the Clans of today, especially when Rock tells him he might find what he's seeking in the mountains. And even if he isn't fully rewarded for his efforts, you have to respect if not admire the lengths he's willing to go (especially for a blind cat) and the amount of time he's willing to take in order to find the answers he's seeking. Even if he is still a grump, his curiosity and determination and passion for knowledge make him so likable and even relatable (for someone like me). Plus, given how grumpy he usually is, it only makes the interactions with his siblings that much sweeter. You can tell that he really does love and care about them, and not just because they're part of the prophecy like he is.<br /><br />Hollypaw – Once again, even if I'm willing to admit that Jaypaw is arguably the main character in this book, Hollypaw is the sibling I connected the most to. The way she thinks about things and feels about things I thought was very similar to mine. She's passionate about defending the vulnerable and weak, yet she feels a bit of peer pressure to have a mate and kits, even though she doesn't feel called to such a life and that it would only be a roadblock to what she really wants. Her consideration of the future and how she can best serve her Clan leads to her desire be the kind of leader her grandfather is – a strong (both physically and mentally), wise, and experienced one who cares not just for her Clan as a whole but every individual cat in it, yet also cares about the other Clans enough to only use violence as a last resort. This is why she's drawn to the mountains – so that she can both learn about and learn from the customs and traditions of the Tribe of Rushing Water in order to make herself a more effective leader. Even if her ambitions aren't always realistic, I liked that it made her feel rather mature for her age. Yet the story cares to remind us of her actual age when she goes off with Lionpaw and Breezepaw to the barn, where they end up having to be rescued. Plus it was funny to read how she rolls her eyes at the way Honeypaw fawns over Berrynose.<br /><br />Lionpaw – I really liked how much more development Lionpaw got here compared to the first two books in the "Power of Three" arc. Not that his development wasn't good in those, far from it! Maybe it's because he (in my opinion) has never really been the main character so far in this arc like his brother and sister have been. That said, I like how the amount of time given to each sibling felt pretty evenly distributed here. Moreover, I really liked how they were all interesting in their own way. Whereas Jaypaw is a deep-thinking healer and Hollypaw wants to use her wisdom and experience to benefit her Clan, Lionpaw is very much a warrior in the truest sense of the word. He relishes physical activity and valiantly fighting on behalf of not just his Clan but the Tribe cats as well. He has lofty ambitions and wants to be the greatest warrior ThunderClan has ever known, and sees the mountains as a gateway to a world of adventure. But at the same time, he has yet to learn that ambition can also be dangerous, given he still interacts with Tigerstar and Hawkfrost and has moments when their influence over him shows – particularly in his fight with his mentor Ashfur, and the final battle against the intruders. I just hopes he learns that aforementioned lesson soon because I like him too much to lose him to the Dark Forest!<br /><br />Breezepaw – Thank StarClan (and/or the Tribe of Endless Hunting, whichever you prefer) that Breezepaw is not the main character despite being on the cover of the version I read! Not that he's a bad character. If anything, he's remarkably well-written despite how much of a whiner and a pain in the tail he can be. That said, he doesn't whine or complain so much that it's maddening. In fact, I found those moments well-timed and even kinda funny, given that each was spaced widely enough from the one before it. Still, while I will give him credit in that he is a capable warrior and loyal enough to the ones he's working with, he definitely has an attitude problem like his father before him, except it's worse. Speaking of which, however, I like that I did feel some sympathy toward him when I learned that he and Crowfeather don't get along all that well. That's what I like about characters like these when they're written by Erin Hunter. Even their most unlikable characters are not intolerable. I just hope Breezepaw at least somewhat matures from this experience in the mountains.<br /><br />Brambleclaw and Stoneteller – Ever since I wrapped up the "New Prophecy" arc, I did kinda miss him, even as I got to know and enjoy his kits (or so he thinks). It felt great to see him back in action with the other main players of the previous arc. And once again, he proves himself a more than worthy deputy and successor of Firestar. I felt for how frustrated he got when he was trying to come up with ways to help the Tribe, yet I rooted for him the whole time because I'd read about how good of a leader he already showed himself to be. I also really liked his interactions with Lionpaw, though they were kind of bittersweet. You could very well believe these two were father and son. But since I know Crowfeather is really Lionpaw's father, there was a faint trace of sadness to it all. That all said, it also felt great to once again visit the Tribe of Rushing Water, even if their circumstances were great in another kind of way. Even if I sometimes got frustrated with Stoneteller and stubbornness (especially when he banished Stormfur and Brook), I also felt the burden on his shoulders. His Tribe is on the brink of desolation, and his faith in the Tribe of Endless Hunting wavers to the point where he's willing to lie to his Tribe about what they said, simply because he can't stand the state of hopelessness they're in. Even if he is sometimes a bit too strict about things, you can tell he legit loves and cares for his Tribe and it pains him to see them like this. And even if he is stubbornly doubtful of and hesitant to implement the customs of the Clans, you have to remember that the Tribe has done things their own way for generations. Old traditions die hard after all.<br /><br />Various Other Characters – It felt great to see the team from the "New Prophecy" arc working together again, even if they aren't featured as much. Squirrelflight is now a wise and experienced warrior. The story of how Stormfur and Brook got banished really made me feel for them. But honestly, I was probably most happy to see Tawnypelt return. It felt like she kinda disappeared in the last two books. Not that it bothered me a lot; it was just something I noticed. That said, it's really cool that she's now a mother, and rather interesting that she named one of her kits Tigerkit. As for Crowfeather, while I do believe he has mostly moved on from his first two romances that failed and that he'll be always be a capable warrior, I couldn't help but wonder why he wasn't willing to get along with Breezepaw. I still like Crowfeather's character and always will, but that part about him felt pretty sad to me. Purdy as well was a pleasant surprise. I liked how sweet Hollypaw was toward him and how he gets a moment of awesomeness when he saves her, Lionpaw, and Breezepaw from the dogs. Moving on though, like I said, getting back to the Tribe again felt great! I seriously respect Talon and Night for risking their own banishment by going to the Clans for help. I found Pebble, one of the to-bes, endearing. And Crag's determination and loyalty to his Tribe really made him stand out to me as a potentially great leader. Stripes and his cats truly frustrated me to no end, even though I do wish we knew a little bit more of their backstory. And Rock I think is probably the most unique character in the series, not just because he looks like a Sphynx cat (the main breed of hairless cat in the real world). You get the sense that he truly lived in a time long past, while also feeling some sense of wonder at how ancient and wise he is.<br /><br />Overall: I honestly wasn't really expecting to like this book as much as I did. Not that I was expecting to dislike it; I just didn't think it would give me a mind-blowing realization. I'm halfway through the "Power of Three" arc, and the fourth title, "Eclipse," is one I've been waiting to read for weeks! I can't wait to see how everything that happened here leads into that next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12055670991042795122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2576380057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576380057" />
    <a title="jess  (bibliophilicjester)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26969694-jess-bibliophilicjester"><img alt="jess  (bibliophilicjester)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453089249p2/26969694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576380057?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jess  (bibliophilicjester)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jess  (bibliophilicjester)" href="/user/show/26969694-jess-bibliophilicjester">jess  (bibliophilicjester)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062367105" href="/book/show/23367399-outcast">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576380057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17780701394563201837">Well that was just a cruel cliffhanger of an ending, and I'm a bit bitter, so 3.75 stars lol <br/><br/>Sometimes I have to remind myself with the larger warriors universe and the 6 book arcs, these are sort of stories within stories. Also, they're meant for kids or at least younger readers are the target, so the books won't always stop when I expect. From the tiny blurb on the back of the book, it seems like the whole thing will be a journey...but that doesn't start until halfway through. Which felt weird</span>
  <span id="freeText17780701394563201837" style="display:none">Well that was just a cruel cliffhanger of an ending, and I'm a bit bitter, so 3.75 stars lol <br /><br />Sometimes I have to remind myself with the larger warriors universe and the 6 book arcs, these are sort of stories within stories. Also, they're meant for kids or at least younger readers are the target, so the books won't always stop when I expect. From the tiny blurb on the back of the book, it seems like the whole thing will be a journey...but that doesn't start until halfway through. Which felt weird to me, because why wouldn't you just tack on the beginning bit to book 2, then start 3 with the journey? But really...we journeyed, we got to the destination, we did some things and learned some things...and everything else is a big question mark. Which is def how you get readers excited for the next book. We got some answers, but I have SO many more questions. <br /><br />Jaypaw is by far my favorite of the three. I find lionpaw really tedious to follow. But...I wanted to take a minute to appreciate hollypaw in this book. She's so torn about everything, and I think we all feel that sense of trying and flailing in the shit storm that is 2020. There's a point toward the beginning where she sees her friend crushing on another cat, and she thinks, why is she thinking about taking a mate already? And then she realizes she doesn't want to be expected to have kits for the clan, she just wants to be a warrior. Or does she? She gets kind of overwhelmed by warrior training because it's a lot at once, and I understand that so much. She decides to focus on just getting better at hunting for a while, and is really hard on herself for sloppy kills. But through lionpaw, we see she's a really good hunter - much more skilled than she gives herself credit for. She wants everything or nothing, she wants to be a leader, or a medicine cat, or a warrior, and not a mother...and she throws herself into her decisions 100%, even if she changes her mind later. I think I like her more with every book I read. <br /><br />I'm not sure if I'm just looking for it more now, but this arc seems to deal a lot with mental health although it's not directly mentioned. Also, jaypaw's grumpiness and staring into space just being introspective is more relatable than most human characters I've read. I'm just saying. I also love how in outcast especially, he's so like secretly ambitious. He wants to learn all the secrets and know all the things and have all the power, but he's doing it in his own way. <br /><br />It's also kind of funny how jumpy they all still are about tigerstar. Someone has a white kit and it's cloudkit, a gray one might be sootkit or something...but star clan forbid you call a cat with stripes tigerkit. Like only one evil dude will ever have a claim to a name that refers to stripes lol I can't handle their drama sometimes hahaha</span>
  <a data-text-id="17780701394563201837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3636313329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3636313329" />
    <a title="Marisa Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55478447-marisa-rose"><img alt="Marisa Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564708769p2/55478447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3636313329?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marisa Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marisa Rose" href="/user/show/55478447-marisa-rose">Marisa Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3636313329&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3636313329" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3922682669014993452">Dumbest cliff-hanger ever. Not even a cliff-hanger, but it’s wrapped like one so it’s still dumb.<br/><br/>This is, without a doubt, the worst Warriors book I’ve read so far. There is absolutely no point to this entire book. At least The Sun Trail (the last book I said was the worst Warriors book) had a point, even though it was written so badly. <br/><br/>What happened in this book, then?<br/><br/>Well, a couple Tribe cats showed up to collect Brook and Stormfur because the Tribe is too helpless to fight back against a rand</span>
  <span id="freeText3922682669014993452" style="display:none">Dumbest cliff-hanger ever. Not even a cliff-hanger, but it’s wrapped like one so it’s still dumb.<br /><br />This is, without a doubt, the worst Warriors book I’ve read so far. There is absolutely no point to this entire book. At least The Sun Trail (the last book I said was the worst Warriors book) had a point, even though it was written so badly. <br /><br />What happened in this book, then?<br /><br />Well, a couple Tribe cats showed up to collect Brook and Stormfur because the Tribe is too helpless to fight back against a random group of intruders that want to settle in the mountains for some reason. It’s mentioned a lot how the mountains are completely inhospitable, that it’s crazy a group of cats lives there, etc, so I find it hard to believe an entire other group of cats is just dying to steal their territory. At no point is it ever explained what these cats are doing there and what’s going to happen to the Tribe after the Clan cats leave. In fact, it’s even stated at the end of the book that even the Tribe’s ancestors are pretty much expecting them to fail eventually. All the Clan cats seem to agree that the Tribe isn’t capable of defending their borders alone, so they’re heroes today but next time there’s a fight and the Clan cats have left, they know the Tribe is pretty much done for. And they’re all like... okay with it. Why??? There is nothing satisfying about this book, nothing that ties it all together, nothing that resolves anything. <br /><br />So what did it accomplish in regard to the rest of the series? NOTHING! At the end of the book, Jaypaw says they were all meant to come to the mountains, not to save the Tribe, but because the Three were supposed to go to the mountains at some point. Why? That’s not explained either. Like, look, I’m cool with some level of mystery around the plot or whatever, but telling your audience at the end of the book “There was no point to all of this” is just worrisome. <br /><br />There was absolutely no need for this installment. Jaypaw could have learned some other way that the ancient cats he’s been dreaming about are the Tribe’s ancestors as well. There’s no reason he couldn’t have dreamed this and avoided the plot with the Tribe altogether. I feel like we were robbed of a book with an actual promising premise—Jaypaw unraveling the mystery of how the ancient cats in his dreams are connected to the present, and how it’ll affect his future and his siblings’ futures. <br /><br />Once again, TenelleFlowers’ take on The Power of Three is living rent-free in my head... wish it was canon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3922682669014993452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094781154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14045445534322053619">Warriors Outcast is a wild fantastic tale of a community of feral cats.<br/><br/>This book is a part of the series “Warriors: Power of Three”.<br/>In this book, all three of the main characters travel to the mountains to help the mountain tribe of feral cats. Throughout the book, you never know what's going to happen next because the story keeps you on your toes the whole time.<br/><br/>This is a fantasy book and is 317 pages. It is a pleasantly challenging read. The author is Erin Hunter. I think that this book is exce</span>
  <span id="freeText14045445534322053619" style="display:none">Warriors Outcast is a wild fantastic tale of a community of feral cats.<br /><br />This book is a part of the series “Warriors: Power of Three”.<br />In this book, all three of the main characters travel to the mountains to help the mountain tribe of feral cats. Throughout the book, you never know what's going to happen next because the story keeps you on your toes the whole time.<br /><br />This is a fantasy book and is 317 pages. It is a pleasantly challenging read. The author is Erin Hunter. I think that this book is exceptional compared to books of the same genre.<br /><br />This book tells the story of these feline mountain invaders. The invaders are cats that are trying to steal the mountain cats' home. The forest cats go to the mountains to try and stop the invaders because they are friends with the mountain cats but the mountain cats don't want them there. So, how can the forest cats help the mountain cats when the mountain cats don't even want help? To find out, you have to read the book.<br /><br />The main characters are Jaypaw, Lionpaw and Hollypaw. Jaypaw can read minds and is blind but he also has a deep connection with his ancestors. Hollypaw is one of the best hunters in the forest. Lionpaw is a great fighter and also has a connection with his evil grandfather and uncle who are in an interesting predicament. These characters have conflicts that are so relatable that you forget they are not real people, let alone cats. They are likable and understandable and they are all brothers and sisters that work together to face their problems.<br /><br />My favorite character in the story was Jaypaw. Why? You must read the story to find out because the reasons become obvious. This book might help you realize the troubles you feel deep down inside and help you deal with it because the main characters are dealing with troubles too. This is set in the present-day forest and in the mountains. It is mostly realistic with elements of fantasy, like animals that can talk. You can easily imagine the picturesque story in your mind.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book because it throws you into the life of an animal and I think you'll like that part too. It is for readers10 years old and up. After reading this book, I am excited for the next one.<br />Reviewed by: Jace O, age 10, Tidewater Mensa</span>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2539976466&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539976466" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13982098793004285207">This is the first book in this entire series that I'm giving less than a perfect rating. Two reasons for that:<br/><br/>1. I first read this series when I was in middle school and continued with it through high school, and this was the last book of the series I read before I gave up on it. It just wasn't as good as the previous books in The Power of Three cycle, or even The New Prophecy/Firestar's Propecy cycles. I didn't even realize it until just before finishing this book, but Firestar and Leafpool hav</span>
  <span id="freeText13982098793004285207" style="display:none">This is the first book in this entire series that I'm giving less than a perfect rating. Two reasons for that:<br /><br />1. I first read this series when I was in middle school and continued with it through high school, and this was the last book of the series I read before I gave up on it. It just wasn't as good as the previous books in The Power of Three cycle, or even The New Prophecy/Firestar's Propecy cycles. I didn't even realize it until just before finishing this book, but Firestar and Leafpool have become my two favorite characters in this series, and because this book takes place with the Tribe cats in the mountains, we don't see Firestar and Leafpool beyond the first chapter or so when the cats are still at the lake. Once we'd left the lake and weren't seeing Firestar and Leafpool anymore, I got bored and stopped reading. And it was the same on my reread, too. It just wasn't as good as the other books in this series and I had to force myself to read it, whereas with the other books in this series, I devoured each of them in one sitting. This one, I had to force myself to slog through it. But it's still a fun story and a good addition to the series. <br /><br />2. This book focuses on the conflict between the Tribe and the intruders who have come to try and take over the mountains. We see the three apprentices, along with the original five cats who made the journey, help the Tribe battle the intruders and make peace with them. Yet we never actually learn why the intruders came to begin with, or why they were so antagonistic toward the Tribe yet gave up so easily as soon as the Clan cats took the battle to the intruders' nests. And the next book, the Clan cats go back to the lake without learning about the intruders' origins, how they came to the mountains, and why they're so antagonistic toward the Tribe. It's just a huge plot hole left unresolved and it leaves me with a bad taste in my mouth. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3474523859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9685157964918769099">Tribe cats come to ask the Clans for help. Jaypaw "sees" Brook's memories and knows he, Lionpaw, and Hollypaw must go on the quest to the mountains. As Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight gather the cats from the other Clans who went on the first journey, the apprentices ask to go. As the group goes to the mountains, they meet old friends along the way and try to help the best they can. Jaypaw knows the truth but hasn't revealed it yet.<br/><br/>I am so into these books. This series, by far, is the best. I cou</span>
  <span id="freeText9685157964918769099" style="display:none">Tribe cats come to ask the Clans for help. Jaypaw "sees" Brook's memories and knows he, Lionpaw, and Hollypaw must go on the quest to the mountains. As Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight gather the cats from the other Clans who went on the first journey, the apprentices ask to go. As the group goes to the mountains, they meet old friends along the way and try to help the best they can. Jaypaw knows the truth but hasn't revealed it yet.<br /><br />I am so into these books. This series, by far, is the best. I could not put this book down. I want to know about the ancient tribes that were in the Clan area as well as the Tribe area. I also want to know why Jaypaw is not letting the others know about his dreams and his ability to walk in others' dreams. I still don't know the answer to that. I want to know about the prophecy Jaypaw received but hasn't revealed to the others who will be affected by the prophecy. And why does Lionpaw have such a strong connection to Tigerstar and Hawkfrost? So many questions, so few answers as of now. I cannot wait to read the next book in The Power of Three series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9685157964918769099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1408328598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10799458937157350837">I don’t really know how I feel about this book. I kind of feel that it was unneeded but readers needed to know that the ancient cats started out at the lake first.<br/><br/>I don’t think the intruders needed to be brought in the way they were although, thinking about it, maybe this led to Stoneteller not picking the next one.<br/><br/>I’m not that big a fan of shock value, especially when it isn’t done right and doesn’t seem to help the story. Rock really doesn’t seem to do anything either but confirm what Jaypaw s</span>
  <span id="freeText10799458937157350837" style="display:none">I don’t really know how I feel about this book. I kind of feel that it was unneeded but readers needed to know that the ancient cats started out at the lake first.<br /><br />I don’t think the intruders needed to be brought in the way they were although, thinking about it, maybe this led to Stoneteller not picking the next one.<br /><br />I’m not that big a fan of shock value, especially when it isn’t done right and doesn’t seem to help the story. Rock really doesn’t seem to do anything either but confirm what Jaypaw suspected.<br /><br />Even though I didn’t really see the point in some of the book, Breezepaw had no growth whatsoever so I guess the only point of him going was to make sure that the other ‘paws were grateful for Brambleclaw. As I was saying, even though I didn’t see the point of some of it, I still enjoyed the book.<br /><br />I really do not like the new cover of this book. Another uncomfortable close up of a cat giving the reader the side-eye.<br /><br />Other than that, I did enjoy the writing, it was very engaging and the plot had a nice, steady pace to it.<br /><br />Thank you for reading my review.<br /><br />-Sam</span>
  <a data-text-id="10799458937157350837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tQDDOVoJW8f/vcd3Hn8hsGtSzlxWXUcqZM7dJmTCWrXl1FFgnlxhI5JoTJNmvxF0SvPIQtnhxM2uuOZxIsreBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Mr4zlgxMTzXg9NoA9XRMiX5tj0vooKbjXiPhH1MH8BNiaqHPyBl10Y0hUeSNtHxNX8yJVWccJQSUVdpIFQ90oQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText10912946660679683490" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
